## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models stress as a function of strain and temperature, which is a classic constitutive relationship in materials science. Temperature typically modifies elastic moduli and flow stress through thermal softening or thermally activated mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain without temperature)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic + plastic hardening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Exponential hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(-c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 - c3 * T) (saturating hardening with temperature dependence)
- Arrhenius thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (1/T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Linear thermoelastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon - c1 * T (mechanical strain minus thermal stress contribution)
- Polynomial thermal dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature dependence of modulus)
- Zerilli-Armstrong type: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 * exp(-c3 * T) (BCC/FCC thermally activated flow stress)
- Combined exponential: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(-c1 * T) (exponential thermal softening with linear strain)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (general power-law form)
- Hyperbolic sine flow: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 / T)) (Garofalo/Sellars-Tegart creep model)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → Multiplicative factor (c0 - c1*T) or exp(-c*T) applied to stress-strain relationship
- Strain hardening saturation → Voce-type (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) structure indicates dislocation density saturation
- Thermally activated deformation → Arrhenius-type exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) terms coupling temperature to flow stress
- Separable strain-temperature dependence → Product form f(epsilon)*g(T) when strain hardening and thermal softening are independent mechanisms
- Linear thermal stress contribution → Additive term proportional to T representing thermal expansion mismatch or thermal stress
- Transition from elastic to plastic → Sum of linear term (c*epsilon) and power-law term (c*epsilon**n) representing dual-regime behavior
- Homologous temperature scaling → Temperature appears as (c0 - T) or (1 - c*T) representing distance from melting point
- Rate-independent power-law creep → sigma proportional to epsilon**c with c < 1 indicating work hardening with diminishing returns

- `exp(c*sin(...))` is periodic
